<p><i><b>Enchanted</b></i> is a 2007 American <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Live-action_film" title="Live-action film">live-action</a>/<a href="/wiki/Animation" title="Animation">animated</a> <a href="/wiki/Musical_film" title="Musical film">musical</a> <a href="/wiki/Fantasy_film" title="Fantasy film">fantasy</a> <a href="/wiki/Romantic_comedy_film" title="Romantic comedy film">romantic comedy film</a>, produced by <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Walt Disney Pictures</a> with New York Academy <a href="/wiki/Barry_Sonnenfeld" title="Barry Sonnenfeld">Barry Sonnenfeld</a> and Josephson Entertainment. Written by <a href="/wiki/Bill_Kelly_(writer)" title="Bill Kelly (writer)">Bill Kelly</a> and directed by <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Lima" title="Kevin Lima">Kevin Lima</a>, the film stars <a href="/wiki/Amy_Adams" title="Amy Adams">Amy Adams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Dempsey" title="Patrick Dempsey">Patrick Dempsey</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Marsden" title="James Marsden">James Marsden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Timothy_Spall" title="Timothy Spall">Timothy Spall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Idina_Menzel" title="Idina Menzel">Idina Menzel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rachel_Covey" title="Rachel Covey">Rachel Covey</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Susan_Sarandon" title="Susan Sarandon">Susan Sarandon</a>. The plot focuses on Giselle, an archetypal <a href="/wiki/Disney_Princess" title="Disney Princess">Disney Princess</a>, who is forced from her traditional animated world of Andalasia into the live-action world of New York City. <i>Enchanted</i> was the first Disney film to be distributed by <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_Motion_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Studios Motion Pictures">Walt Disney Studios Motion Pictures</a>, instead of <a href="/wiki/Buena_Vista_(brand)" title="Buena Vista (brand)">Buena Vista Pictures Distribution</a>.</p>
<p>The film is both a <a href="/wiki/Homage_(arts)" title="Homage (arts)">homage</a> to, and a self-<a href="/wiki/Parody_film" title="Parody film">parody</a> of, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Walt_Disney_Animation_Studios_films" title="List of Walt Disney Animation Studios films">Disney's animated features</a>, making numerous references to Disney's past works through the combination of live-action filmmaking, <a href="/wiki/Traditional_animation" title="Traditional animation">traditional animation</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery" title="Computer-generated imagery">computer-generated imagery</a>. It marks the return of traditional animation to a Disney feature film after the company's decision to move entirely to computer animation in 2004. Composer <a href="/wiki/Alan_Menken" title="Alan Menken">Alan Menken</a> and lyricist <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Schwartz_(composer)" title="Stephen Schwartz (composer)">Stephen Schwartz</a>, who had written songs for previous Disney films, produced the songs of <i>Enchanted</i>, with Menken also composing its score.</p>
<p>The animation sequences were produced at <a href="/wiki/James_Baxter_(animator)" title="James Baxter (animator)">James Baxter</a> Animation in Pasadena. Filming of the live action segments took place around New York City. It premiered on October 20, 2007, at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_Film_Festival" title="London Film Festival">London Film Festival</a> before its <a href="/wiki/Wide_release" title="Wide release">wide release</a> on November 21, 2007, in the United States. <i>Enchanted</i> was well-received critically, established Adams as a leading lady, and earned more than $340 million worldwide at the box office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOMojo_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-BOMojo-3">[3]</a></sup> It won three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saturn_Awards" title="Saturn Awards">Saturn Awards</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award_for_Best_Fantasy_Film" title="Saturn Award for Best Fantasy Film">Best Fantasy Film</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Saturn Award for Best Actress">Best Actress</a> for Adams. <i>Enchanted</i> also received two nominations at the <a href="/wiki/65th_Golden_Globe_Awards" title="65th Golden Globe Awards">65th Golden Globe Awards</a> and three <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Academy Award for Best Original Song">Best Original Song</a> nominations at the <a href="/wiki/80th_Academy_Awards" title="80th Academy Awards">80th Academy Awards</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">Plot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enchanted_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Plot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Animated_cartoon" title="Animated cartoon">animated</a> <a href="/wiki/Fairy_tale" title="Fairy tale">fairy tale</a> kingdom of Andalasia, the evil Queen Narissa schemes to protect her claim to the throne, which she will lose once her stepson, Prince Edward, finds his <a href="/wiki/Chivalric_romance" title="Chivalric romance">true love</a> and marries her. She enlists her loyal henchman Nathaniel to keep Edward distracted. Giselle, a young woman, dreams of meeting a prince and experiencing a "<a href="/wiki/Happy_ending" title="Happy ending">happy ever after</a>". Edward hears Giselle singing and sets off to find her. Nathaniel sets free a captured <a href="/wiki/Troll" title="Troll">troll</a> to kill Giselle, but Edward rescues her in time. When they meet, they instantly fall in love and plan to get married the following day.</p>
<p>Narissa, disguised as an old hag, intercepts Giselle on her way to the wedding and pushes her into a well, and she is magically transformed into a 3D live version of herself and transported to a <a href="/wiki/Manhole" title="Manhole">manhole</a> in New York City's <a href="/wiki/Times_Square" title="Times Square">Times Square</a>. Giselle quickly becomes lost. Meanwhile, Robert, a divorce lawyer, prepares to propose to his longtime girlfriend Nancy, much to the dismay of his daughter Morgan. Robert and Morgan encounter Giselle on their way home, and Robert begrudgingly allows Giselle to stay the night at their apartment at the insistence of Morgan, who instantly trusts Giselle.</p>
<p>Pip, Giselle's best <a href="/wiki/Chipmunk" title="Chipmunk">chipmunk</a> friend from Andalasia, had witnessed Giselle's exile and alerted Edward thereafter, and both embark on a rescue mission to the city, where they too are turned into 3D versions, but Pip is instead in the form of a real chipmunk – therefore, losing the ability to speak. Narissa sends Nathaniel to follow and impede Edward. In a restaurant, Narissa appears to Nathaniel in a soup pot and gives him three poisoned apples to murder Giselle. Pip eavesdrops but is unable to communicate with Edward, as animals cannot speak outside of Andalasia. Nathaniel keeps Pip silenced by imprisoning him in various containers. Meanwhile, after Giselle summons <a href="/wiki/Vermin" title="Vermin">vermin</a> to clean Robert's apartment, Nancy arrives to take Morgan to school. She meets Giselle and then angrily leaves assuming Robert was unfaithful. Robert is initially upset but spends the day with Giselle, knowing she is vulnerable in the city. Giselle questions Robert about his relationship with Nancy and helps the pair reconcile by sending Nancy an invitation to the "King and Queen's Costume Ball" at the <a href="/wiki/Woolworth_Building" title="Woolworth Building">Woolworth Building</a>. She also begins to win Robert over with her sunny disposition and optimism, even inadvertently helping one of his clients reconcile with his wife.</p>
<p>After searching throughout the city, Edward finally locates Giselle at Robert's apartment. While Edward is eager to take Giselle home to Andalasia and marry, she insists that they should first go on a date to get to know each other, still conflicted about her feelings. Giselle promises to return to Andalasia after ending their date at the ball, which Robert and Nancy also attend. Narissa, who has been spying from Andalasia, decides to follow and kill Giselle herself after Nathaniel failed to poison her twice. Robert and Giselle share a dance with each other, with both Edward and Nancy noticing their obvious attraction to each other. Giselle and Edward then prepare to leave, but Giselle feels sorrow at leaving Robert behind. Narissa appears as the old hag and offers the last poisoned apple to Giselle, promising "sweet dreams and happy endings." Giselle takes a bite and falls to the floor unconscious.</p>
<p>Narissa attempts to escape with Giselle's body but is stopped by Edward. Nathaniel, realizing Narissa was using him and never loved him, reveals her plot. Robert realizes that true love's kiss (something Giselle often discussed) is the only force powerful enough to break the apple's spell. After Edward's kiss fails to wake Giselle, he prompts Robert to do so instead. Robert kisses her just as the clock strikes twelve, Giselle awakens and the whole crowd cheers, with everyone else believing that the situation is a staged event for the ball. Narissa, however, furiously transforms into a giant blue <a href="/wiki/Dragon" title="Dragon">dragon</a> and takes Robert hostage, prompting much panic throughout the crowd. Giselle takes Edward's sword and pursues Narissa to the top of the building. Pip, who was freed by Edward, helps Giselle successfully defeat Narissa, who falls off of the building to the ground and explodes into magic glitter on impact.</p>
<p>A happy new life unfolds for everyone, showing Edward and Nancy - now animated - marrying in Andalasia; Giselle running a successful fashion business and forming a happy family with Robert and Morgan; while Nathaniel and Pip each become successful authors about their personal experiences in the real world, leaving everyone with their own "happily ever after".</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cast">Cast</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enchanted_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Cast">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Amy_Adams" title="Amy Adams">Amy Adams</a> as Giselle<br/>
A princess-to-be who ends up almost having her dream of meeting her prince a reality. Adams was announced to have been cast in the role of Giselle on November 14, 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> Although the studio was looking for a film star in the role, director Kevin Lima insisted on casting a lesser-known actress. Out of the 300 or so actresses who auditioned for the role,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFW-2007nov20_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-SFW-2007nov20-5">[5]</a></sup> Adams stood out to Lima because not only did she look like "a <a href="/wiki/Disney_Princess" title="Disney Princess">Disney princess</a>" but her "commitment to the character, her ability to escape into the character's being without ever judging the character was overwhelming."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Hailing from Andalasia, Giselle displays similar traits to the <a href="/wiki/Disney_Princess" title="Disney Princess">Disney Princesses</a>; Lima describes her as "about 80% <a href="/wiki/Snow_White_(Disney)" title="Snow White (Disney)">Snow White</a>, with some traits borrowed from <a href="/wiki/Cinderella_(Disney_character)" title="Cinderella (Disney character)">Cinderella</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aurora_(Disney_character)" title="Aurora (Disney character)">Princess Aurora</a> from <i><a href="/wiki/Sleeping_Beauty_(1959_film)" title="Sleeping Beauty (1959 film)">Sleeping Beauty</a></i>... although her spunkiness comes from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ariel_(Disney_character)" title="Ariel (Disney character)">Princess Ariel</a> from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Little_Mermaid_(1989_film)" title="The Little Mermaid (1989 film)">The Little Mermaid</a></i>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAToday-2007nov14_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday-2007nov14-7">[7]</a></sup> She is "eternally optimistic and romantic" but is also "very independent and true to her convictions".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAToday-2007nov14_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday-2007nov14-7">[7]</a></sup> Over the course of the film, she becomes more mature but maintains her innocence and optimism.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Patrick_Dempsey" title="Patrick Dempsey">Patrick Dempsey</a> as Robert<br/>
A cynical, New York City divorce attorney who does not believe in true love or happily-ever-after, or that Giselle understands his daughter, Morgan. Lima cast Dempsey after Disney was satisfied with the casting of Adams but had wanted more well-known actors in the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFW-2007nov20_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-SFW-2007nov20-5">[5]</a></sup> Dempsey, whose starring role on TV series <i><a href="/wiki/Grey%27s_Anatomy" title="Grey's Anatomy">Grey's Anatomy</a></i> had earned him the nickname "McDreamy", was described by Lima as "a modern-day Prince Charming to today's audience".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFW-2007nov20_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-SFW-2007nov20-5">[5]</a></sup> The role was challenging for Dempsey because he had to play the <a href="/wiki/Double_act" title="Double act">straight man</a> to Adams and Marsden's more outrageous characters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THR-2007nov14_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-THR-2007nov14-8">[8]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/James_Marsden" title="James Marsden">James Marsden</a> as Prince Edward<br/>
A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Narcissistic" title="Narcissistic">narcissistic</a> and athletic, yet good-hearted, prince who ends up confused with the world of New York once entering it. Marsden was announced to have been cast on December 6, 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> At the time Marsden was auditioning, the role of Robert had not been cast but he decided to pursue the role of Prince Edward because he was "more fun and he responded more to that character."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Orange-Marsden_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Orange-Marsden-10">[10]</a></sup> Edward is a prince in Andalasia and the stepson of Narissa. He is "very pure, very simple-minded and naive, but innocently narcissistic."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Orange-Marsden_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Orange-Marsden-10">[10]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Timothy_Spall" title="Timothy Spall">Timothy Spall</a> as Nathaniel<br/>
Nathaniel is a servant of Queen Narissa, who controls him through his infatuation with her and his own lack of self-esteem. He initially does Narissa's bidding, but ultimately realizes her true nature and rebels against her. He has a penchant for disguises. This is the first of two Disney films Timothy Spall has been in, the other being Tim Burton's <i><a href="/wiki/Alice_in_Wonderland_(2010_film)" title="Alice in Wonderland (2010 film)">Alice in Wonderland</a></i> in which he was the voice of Bayard the Bloodhound.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Idina_Menzel" title="Idina Menzel">Idina Menzel</a> as Nancy Tremaine<br/>
Robert's fiancee. Once Giselle falls in love with Robert, she falls for Edward and leaves with him. Menzel, who is well known for her Broadway musical roles in <i><a href="/wiki/Wicked_(musical)" title="Wicked (musical)">Wicked</a></i> (whose composer, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Schwartz_(composer)" title="Stephen Schwartz (composer)">Stephen Schwartz</a>, wrote the lyrics to the film's songs) and <i><a href="/wiki/Rent_(musical)" title="Rent (musical)">Rent</a></i>, was offered the role of Nancy Tremaine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFWire-2007nov13_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-SFWire-2007nov13-11">[11]</a></sup> Since the role did not require any singing, Menzel said in an interview that "it was a compliment to be asked to just be hired on her acting talents alone."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Nancy is a fashion designer and Robert's girlfriend. She is named after <a href="/wiki/List_of_Disney%27s_Cinderella_characters#Lady_Tremaine" title="List of Disney's Cinderella characters">Lady Tremaine</a>, the stepmother from <i><a href="/wiki/Cinderella_(1950_film)" title="Cinderella (1950 film)">Cinderella</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAToday-2007nov22-New_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday-2007nov22-New-13">[13]</a></sup> Menzel went on to play a <a href="/wiki/Disney_Princess" title="Disney Princess">Disney Princess</a>: <a href="/wiki/Elsa_(Disney)" title="Elsa (Disney)">Elsa, the Snow Queen</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Frozen_(2013_film)" title="Frozen (2013 film)">Frozen</a></i>, during which she worked with director <a href="/wiki/Chris_Buck" title="Chris Buck">Chris Buck</a>, who previously directed <i><a href="/wiki/Tarzan_(1999_film)" title="Tarzan (1999 film)">Tarzan</a></i> with Lima in 1999.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rachel_Covey" title="Rachel Covey">Rachel Covey</a> as Morgan<br/>
Morgan is Robert's six-year-old daughter. Despite her father misunderstanding her and telling her otherwise, she believes in fairy tales and believes that magic exists.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Susan_Sarandon" title="Susan Sarandon">Susan Sarandon</a> as Queen Narissa<br/>
Queen Narissa is Edward's evil stepmother, sorceress, and a megalomaniac with a hatred for Giselle simply for being an obstacle for her to keep her power. Sarandon had been attracted to the project prior to Lima's involvement as director. Since Sarandon's on-screen time was relatively short, it took only two weeks to film her scenes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AICN-2007dec14_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-AICN-2007dec14-14">[14]</a></sup> Narissa's mannerisms, characteristics, powers, and physical features were inspired by such classical <a href="/wiki/Disney_Villains" title="Disney Villains">Disney villains</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Evil_Queen_(Disney)" title="Evil Queen (Disney)">Evil Queen</a> from <i><a href="/wiki/Snow_White_and_the_Seven_Dwarfs_(1937_film)" title="Snow White and the Seven Dwarfs (1937 film)">Snow White and the Seven Dwarfs</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Maleficent" title="Maleficent">Maleficent</a> from <i><a href="/wiki/Sleeping_Beauty_(1959_film)" title="Sleeping Beauty (1959 film)">Sleeping Beauty</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAToday-2007nov14_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday-2007nov14-7">[7]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jeff_Bennett" title="Jeff Bennett">Jeff Bennett</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Lima" title="Kevin Lima">Kevin Lima</a> as Pip<br/>
Bennett provided the voice for the hand drawn animated Pip in the animated segment while Lima provided the voice for the computer-generated Pip in the live-action segment. Pip, a <a href="/wiki/Chipmunk" title="Chipmunk">chipmunk</a> friend of Giselle who has no trouble expressing himself through speech in Andalasia, loses his ability to speak in the real world and must communicate by acting.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jon_McLaughlin" title="Jon McLaughlin">Jon McLaughlin</a> as himself<br/>
singing "<a href="/wiki/So_Close_(Jon_McLaughlin_song)" title="So Close (Jon McLaughlin song)">So Close</a>" at the ball while Robert and Giselle dance together as do Edward and Nancy.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fred_Tatasciore" title="Fred Tatasciore">Fred Tatasciore</a> as the Troll from Andalasia who tried to eat Giselle</li>
</ul>
<p>Several actresses/actors who have played characters in Disney films have <a href="/wiki/Cameo_appearance" title="Cameo appearance">cameos</a>:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Paige_O%27Hara" title="Paige O'Hara">Paige O'Hara</a> as Angela<br/>
a soap opera character. O'Hara provided the speaking and singing voice of <a href="/wiki/Belle_(Disney)" title="Belle (Disney)">Belle</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Beauty_and_the_Beast_(1991_film)" title="Beauty and the Beast (1991 film)">Beauty and the Beast</a></i>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jodi_Benson" title="Jodi Benson">Jodi Benson</a> as Sam<br/>
Robert's secretary. Benson provided the speaking and singing voice of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ariel_(Disney_character)" title="Ariel (Disney character)">Ariel</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Little_Mermaid_(1989_film)" title="The Little Mermaid (1989 film)">The Little Mermaid</a></i>; she also voiced the various <a href="/wiki/Barbie" title="Barbie">Barbie</a> dolls in <i><a href="/wiki/Toy_Story_2" title="Toy Story 2">Toy Story 2</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Toy_Story_3" title="Toy Story 3">Toy Story 3</a></i>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Judy_Kuhn" title="Judy Kuhn">Judy Kuhn</a> as Pregnant Woman with Kids<br/>
Kuhn provided the singing voice of the <a href="/wiki/Pocahontas_(character)" title="Pocahontas (character)">title character</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Pocahontas_(1995_film)" title="Pocahontas (1995 film)">Pocahontas</a></i> and its <a href="/wiki/Pocahontas_II:_Journey_to_a_New_World" title="Pocahontas II: Journey to a New World">sequel</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Julie_Andrews" title="Julie Andrews">Julie Andrews</a> as the Narrator<br/>
Andrews played the <a href="/wiki/Mary_Poppins_(character)" title="Mary Poppins (character)">title character</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Mary_Poppins_(film)" title="Mary Poppins (film)">Mary Poppins</a></i> as well as appearing in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Princess_Diaries_(film)" title="The Princess Diaries (film)">The Princess Diaries</a></i> series as Queen Clarisse Renaldi and Michaela Collins</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Isiah_Whitlock_Jr." title="Isiah Whitlock Jr.">Isiah Whitlock Jr.</a> as Mr. Banks<br/>
a male client during a divorce case Isiah later appeared in the 2016 remake of <i><a href="/wiki/Pete%27s_Dragon_(2016_film)" title="Pete's Dragon (2016 film)">Pete's Dragon</a></i> as Sheriff Dentler.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enchanted_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enchanted_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The initial script of <i>Enchanted</i>, written by <a href="/wiki/Bill_Kelly_(writer)" title="Bill Kelly (writer)">Bill Kelly</a>, was bought by Disney's <a href="/wiki/Touchstone_Pictures" title="Touchstone Pictures">Touchstone Pictures</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barry_Sonnenfeld" title="Barry Sonnenfeld">Sonnenfeld</a>/<a href="/wiki/Barry_Josephson" title="Barry Josephson">Josephson</a> Productions for a reported sum of $450,000 in September 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW-2007sep11_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-EW-2007sep11-15">[15]</a></sup> However, it was thought to be unsuitable for <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Walt Disney Pictures</a> because it was "a racier R-rated movie".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> To the frustration of Kelly, the screenplay was rewritten several times, first by Rita Hsiao and then by <a href="/wiki/Todd_Alcott" title="Todd Alcott">Todd Alcott</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW-2007sep11_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-EW-2007sep11-15">[15]</a></sup> The film was initially scheduled to be released in 2002 with <a href="/wiki/Rob_Marshall" title="Rob Marshall">Rob Marshall</a> as director but he withdrew due to "creative differences" between the producers and him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> In 2001, director <a href="/wiki/Jon_Turteltaub" title="Jon Turteltaub">Jon Turteltaub</a> was set to direct the film but he left soon after, later working with Disney and <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Bruckheimer" title="Jerry Bruckheimer">Jerry Bruckheimer</a> on the <i><a href="/wiki/National_Treasure_(franchise)" title="National Treasure (franchise)">National Treasure</a></i> franchise. <a href="/wiki/Adam_Shankman" title="Adam Shankman">Adam Shankman</a> became the film's director in 2003, while <a href="/wiki/Bob_Schooley" title="Bob Schooley">Bob Schooley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mark_McCorkle" title="Mark McCorkle">Mark McCorkle</a> were hired by Disney to rewrite the script once again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> At the time, Disney considered offering the role of Giselle to <a href="/wiki/Kate_Hudson" title="Kate Hudson">Kate Hudson</a> or <a href="/wiki/Reese_Witherspoon" title="Reese Witherspoon">Reese Witherspoon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW-2007sep11_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-EW-2007sep11-15">[15]</a></sup> However, the project did not take off.</p>
<p>On May 25, 2005, <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i> reported that <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Lima" title="Kevin Lima">Kevin Lima</a> had been hired as director and Bill Kelly had returned to the project to write a new version of the script.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Lima worked with Kelly on the script to combine the main plot of <i>Enchanted</i> with the idea of a "loving homage" to Disney's heritage. He created visual storyboard printouts that covered the story of <i>Enchanted</i> from beginning to end, which filled an entire floor of a production building.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> After Lima showed them to <a href="/wiki/Dick_Cook" title="Dick Cook">Dick Cook</a>, the chairman of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Studios_(division)" title="The Walt Disney Studios (division)">Walt Disney Studios</a>, he received the green light for the project and a budget of $85 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BW-2007jul05_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-BW-2007jul05-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AICN-2007dec14_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-AICN-2007dec14-14">[14]</a></sup> Lima began designing the world of Andalasia and storyboarding the movie before a cast was chosen to play the characters. After the actors were hired, he was involved in making the final design of the movie, which made sure the animated characters look like their real-life counterparts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THR-2007nov14_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-THR-2007nov14-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Filming">Filming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enchanted_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Filming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Enchanted</i> is the first feature-length Disney live-action/traditional animation hybrid since Disney's <i><a href="/wiki/Who_Framed_Roger_Rabbit" title="Who Framed Roger Rabbit">Who Framed Roger Rabbit</a></i> in 1988, though the traditionally animated characters do not interact in the live-action environment in the same method as they did in <i>Roger Rabbit</i>; however, there are some scenes where live-action characters share the screen with two-dimensional animated characters, for example, a live-action Nathaniel communicating with a cel-drawn Narissa, who is in a cooking pot. The film uses two <a href="/wiki/Aspect_ratio" title="Aspect ratio">aspect ratios</a>; it begins in 2.35:1 when the <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Walt Disney Pictures</a> logo and <i>Enchanted</i> storybook are shown, and then switches to a smaller 1.85:1 aspect ratio for the first animated sequence. The film switches back to 2.35:1 when it becomes live-action and never switches back, even for the remainder of the cartoon sequences. When this movie was aired on televised networks, the beginning of the movie (minus the logo and opening credits) was shown in standard definition; the remainder of the movie was shown in high definition when it becomes live-action. Lima oversaw the direction of both the live-action and animation sequences, which were being produced at the same time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THR-2007nov14_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-THR-2007nov14-8">[8]</a></sup> <i>Enchanted</i> took almost two years to complete. The animation took about a year to finish while the live-action scenes, which commenced filming on location in New York City during the summer of 2006 and were completed during the animation process, were shot in 72 days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THR-2007nov14_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-THR-2007nov14-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Animation">Animation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enchanted_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Animation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Out of the film's 107 minutes of running time, ten of the approximately 13 minutes of animation are at the beginning of the film. Lima tried to "cram every single piece of Disney iconic imagery" that he could into the first ten minutes, which were done in <a href="/wiki/Traditional_animation" title="Traditional animation">traditional cel animation</a> (in contrast to computer-generated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3-D_animation" title="3-D animation">3-D animation</a>) as a tribute to past Disney fairy tale films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Sleeping_Beauty_(1959_film)" title="Sleeping Beauty (1959 film)">Sleeping Beauty</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Cinderella_(1950_film)" title="Cinderella (1950 film)">Cinderella</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Snow_White_and_the_Seven_Dwarfs_(1937_film)" title="Snow White and the Seven Dwarfs (1937 film)">Snow White and the Seven Dwarfs</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THR-2007nov14_8-4"><a href="#cite_note-THR-2007nov14-8">[8]</a></sup> It was the first Disney film theatrically released in America to feature traditional cel animation since <i><a href="/wiki/Pooh%27s_Heffalump_Movie" title="Pooh's Heffalump Movie">Pooh's Heffalump Movie</a></i> (2005). This film, although quite different in terms of plot from any previous Disney film, also contained obvious homages to other Disney films of the distant past, such as <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Yeller_(1957_film)" title="Old Yeller (1957 film)">Old Yeller</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Shaggy_Dog_(1959_film)" title="The Shaggy Dog (1959 film)">The Shaggy Dog</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swiss_Family_Robinson_(film)" title="Swiss Family Robinson (film)">Swiss Family Robinson</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Bon_Voyage!_(1962_film)" title="Bon Voyage! (1962 film)">Bon Voyage!</a></i>, and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Savage_Sam" title="Savage Sam">Savage Sam</a></i>. As most of Disney's cel animation artists were laid off after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CG_artwork" title="CG artwork">computer graphics</a> boom of the late 1990s,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> the 13 minutes of animation were not done in-house but by the independent <a href="/wiki/Pasadena,_California" title="Pasadena, California">Pasadena</a>-based company <a href="/wiki/James_Baxter_(animator)" title="James Baxter (animator)">James Baxter</a> Animation, which was started by noted lead <a href="/wiki/Animator" title="Animator">animator</a> <a href="/wiki/James_Baxter_(animator)" title="James Baxter (animator)">James Baxter</a>. Baxter had previously worked for <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Animation_Studios" title="Walt Disney Animation Studios">Walt Disney Animation Studios</a>, bringing to life many memorable Disney animated characters like <a href="/wiki/List_of_Who_Framed_Roger_Rabbit_characters#Jessica_Rabbit" title="List of Who Framed Roger Rabbit characters">Jessica Rabbit</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Who_Framed_Roger_Rabbit" title="Who Framed Roger Rabbit">Who Framed Roger Rabbit</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Belle_(Disney)" title="Belle (Disney)">Belle</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Beauty_and_the_Beast_(1991_film)" title="Beauty and the Beast (1991 film)">Beauty and the Beast</a></i>), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_The_Lion_King_characters#Rafiki" title="List of The Lion King characters">Rafiki</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King" title="The Lion King">The Lion King</a></i>), and <a href="/wiki/Quasimodo" title="Quasimodo">Quasimodo</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Hunchback_of_Notre_Dame_(1996_film)" title="The Hunchback of Notre Dame (1996 film)">The Hunchback of Notre Dame</a></i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAToday-2007nov14_7-3"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday-2007nov14-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although Lima wanted the animation to be <a href="/wiki/Nostalgia" title="Nostalgia">nostalgic</a>, he wanted <i>Enchanted</i> to have a style of its own. Baxter's team decided to use <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">Art Nouveau</a> as a starting point. For Giselle, the hand-drawn animated character had to be "a cross between <a href="/wiki/Amy_Adams" title="Amy Adams">Amy Adams</a> and a classic <a href="/wiki/Disney_Princess" title="Disney Princess">Disney princess</a>. And not a caricature." Seeing Giselle as "a forest girl, an innocent nymph with flowers in her hair" and "a bit of a hippie", the animators wanted her to be "flowing, with her hair and clothes. Delicate."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAToday-2007may02-cast_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday-2007may02-cast-23">[23]</a></sup> For Prince Edward, Baxter's team "worked the hardest on him to make him look like the actor" because princes "in these kinds of movies are usually so bland."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAToday-2007may02-cast_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday-2007may02-cast-23">[23]</a></sup> Many prototypes were made for Narissa as Baxter's team wanted her face to "look like <a href="/wiki/Susan_Sarandon" title="Susan Sarandon">Susan Sarandon</a>. And the costumes had to align closely to the live-action design."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAToday-2007may02-cast_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday-2007may02-cast-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>To maintain continuity between the two media, Lima brought in costume designer Mona May during the early stages of the film's production so the costumes would be aligned in both the animated and live-action worlds. He also shot some live-action footage of Amy Adams as Giselle for the animators to use as reference, which also allowed the physical movement of the character to match in both worlds. Test scenes completed by the animators were shown to the actors, allowing them to see how their animated self would move.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THR-2007nov14_8-5"><a href="#cite_note-THR-2007nov14-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Live-action">Live-action</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enchanted_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Live-action">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Enchanted_(Disney).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Enchanted_%28Disney%29.jpg/220px-Enchanted_%28Disney%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Enchanted_%28Disney%29.jpg/330px-Enchanted_%28Disney%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Enchanted_%28Disney%29.jpg/440px-Enchanted_%28Disney%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Enchanted_(Disney).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Timothy_Spall" title="Timothy Spall">Timothy Spall</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Marsden" title="James Marsden">James Marsden</a> during filming in <a href="/wiki/Columbus_Circle" title="Columbus Circle">Columbus Circle</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Principal photography began in April 2006 and ended in July 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Because of the sequence setting, the live action scenes are filmed in New York City. However, shooting in New York became problematic as it was in a "constant state of new stores, scaffolding and renovation".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first scene in New York, which features Giselle emerging from a manhole in the middle of <a href="/wiki/Times_Square" title="Times Square">Times Square</a>, was filmed on location in the center of the square. Because of the difficulties in controlling the crowd while filming in <a href="/wiki/Times_Square" title="Times Square">Times Square</a>, general pedestrians were featured in the scene with hired extras placed in the immediate foreground.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Similarly, a crowd gathered to watch as <a href="/wiki/James_Marsden" title="James Marsden">James Marsden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timothy_Spall" title="Timothy Spall">Timothy Spall</a> filmed their scenes in <a href="/wiki/Times_Square" title="Times Square">Times Square</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> However, the scene Lima found the most challenging to shoot was the musical number, "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/That%27s_How_You_Know_(musical_number)" title="That's How You Know (musical number)">That's How You Know</a>", in <a href="/wiki/Central_Park" title="Central Park">Central Park</a>. The five-minute scene took 17 days to finish due to the changing weather, which allowed only seven sunny days for the scene to be filmed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THR-2007nov14_8-6"><a href="#cite_note-THR-2007nov14-8">[8]</a></sup> The filming was also hampered at times by <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Dempsey" title="Patrick Dempsey">Patrick Dempsey</a>'s fans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AICN-2007dec14_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-AICN-2007dec14-14">[14]</a></sup> The scene was choreographed by John O'Connell, who had worked on <i><a href="/wiki/Moulin_Rouge!" title="Moulin Rouge!">Moulin Rouge!</a></i> beforehand, and included 300 extras and 150 dancers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THR-2007nov14_8-7"><a href="#cite_note-THR-2007nov14-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many scenes were filmed at <a href="/wiki/Steiner_Studios" title="Steiner Studios">Steiner Studios</a>, which provided the three large stages that <i>Enchanted</i> needed at the same facility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BW-2007jul05_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-BW-2007jul05-2">[2]</a></sup> Other outdoor locations included the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Bridge" title="Brooklyn Bridge">Brooklyn Bridge</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Paterno" title="The Paterno">The Paterno</a>, an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apartment_building" title="Apartment building">apartment building</a> with a curved, heavily embellished, ivory-colored façade located on the corner of <a href="/wiki/Riverside_Drive_(Manhattan)" title="Riverside Drive (Manhattan)">Riverside Drive</a> and <a href="/wiki/116th_Street_(Manhattan)" title="116th Street (Manhattan)">116th Street</a>, which is the residence of the film's characters Robert and Morgan.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Costume_design">Costume design</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enchanted_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Costume design">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Enchanted_costume.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="768" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Enchanted_costume.jpg/170px-Enchanted_costume.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Enchanted_costume.jpg/255px-Enchanted_costume.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Enchanted_costume.jpg/340px-Enchanted_costume.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Enchanted_costume.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Giselle's wedding dress on display at <a href="/wiki/El_Capitan_Theatre" title="El Capitan Theatre">El Capitan Theatre</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>All the costumes in the film were designed by Mona May, who had previously worked on <i><a href="/wiki/Clueless_(film)" title="Clueless (film)">Clueless</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wedding_Singer" title="The Wedding Singer">The Wedding Singer</a>,</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Haunted_Mansion_(film)" title="The Haunted Mansion (film)">The Haunted Mansion</a></i>. To create the costumes, May spent one year in pre-production working with animators and her costume department of 20 people, while she contracted with five outside costume shops in Los Angeles and New York City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ThePlainDealer-2007nov23_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-ThePlainDealer-2007nov23-28">[28]</a></sup> She became involved in the project during the time when the animators are designing the faces and bodies of the characters as they had to "translate the costumes from two-dimensional drawings to live-action human proportion".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TAR-2007nov20_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-TAR-2007nov20-29">[29]</a></sup> Her goal was to keep the designs "Disneyesque to the core but bring a little bit of fashion in there and humor and make it something new".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TAR-2007nov20_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-TAR-2007nov20-29">[29]</a></sup> However, May admitted this was difficult "because they're dealing with iconic Disney characters who have been in the psyche of the viewing audience for so long".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HSB-2007nov15_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-HSB-2007nov15-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>For the character of Giselle, her journey to becoming a real woman is reflected in her dresses, which become less fairy tale-like as the film progresses. Her wedding dress at the beginning of the film directly contrasts her modern <a href="/wiki/Gown" title="Gown">gown</a> at the end of the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ThePlainDealer-2007nov23_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-ThePlainDealer-2007nov23-28">[28]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Wedding_dress" title="Wedding dress">wedding dress</a> served to provide a "humongous contrast to the flat drawings" and to accentuate the image of a <a href="/wiki/Disney_Princess" title="Disney Princess">Disney Princess</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TAR-2007nov20_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-TAR-2007nov20-29">[29]</a></sup> In order to make the waist look small, the <a href="/wiki/Sleeve" title="Sleeve">sleeves</a> are designed to be "extremely pouffy" and the <a href="/wiki/Skirt" title="Skirt">skirt</a> to be as big as possible, which included a metal <a href="/wiki/Hoop_skirt" title="Hoop skirt">hoop</a> that holds up 20 layers of petticoats and ruffles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HSB-2007nov15_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-HSB-2007nov15-30">[30]</a></sup> Altogether, 11 versions of the dress are made for filming, each comprised 200 yards (183 m) of silk satin and other fabric, and weighed approximately 40 pounds (18 kg).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ThePlainDealer-2007nov23_28-2"><a href="#cite_note-ThePlainDealer-2007nov23-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HSB-2007nov15_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-HSB-2007nov15-30">[30]</a></sup> On the experience of wearing the wedding dress, Amy Adams described it as "grueling" since "the entire weight was on her <a href="/wiki/Hip" title="Hip">hips</a>, so occasionally it felt like she was in traction".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>Unlike Giselle, Prince Edward does not adapt to the real world and <a href="/wiki/James_Marsden" title="James Marsden">James Marsden</a>, who plays Edward, had only one costume designed for him. May's aim was to try "not to lose Marsden in the craziness of the outfit... where he still looks handsome".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TAR-2007nov20_29-3"><a href="#cite_note-TAR-2007nov20-29">[29]</a></sup> The costume also included padding in the chest, <a href="/wiki/Buttocks" title="Buttocks">buttocks</a>, and crotch, which gave Marsden the "same exaggerated proportions as an animated character"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ThePlainDealer-2007nov23_28-3"><a href="#cite_note-ThePlainDealer-2007nov23-28">[28]</a></sup> and "posture – his back is straight, the sleeves are up and never collapse".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TAR-2007nov20_29-4"><a href="#cite_note-TAR-2007nov20-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>May was delighted that Lima "went for something more fashion-forward" with <a href="/wiki/Susan_Sarandon" title="Susan Sarandon">Susan Sarandon</a>'s Queen Narissa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ThePlainDealer-2007nov23_28-4"><a href="#cite_note-ThePlainDealer-2007nov23-28">[28]</a></sup> She decided to make her look like a "runway lady",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TAR-2007nov20_29-5"><a href="#cite_note-TAR-2007nov20-29">[29]</a></sup> wearing something that is "still Disney" but also "high fashion, like something <a href="/wiki/John_Galliano" title="John Galliano">John Galliano</a> or <a href="/wiki/Thierry_Mugler" title="Thierry Mugler">Thierry Mugler</a> might design".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HSB-2007nov15_30-3"><a href="#cite_note-HSB-2007nov15-30">[30]</a></sup> Since Narissa appears in three media: <a href="/wiki/Traditional_animation" title="Traditional animation">hand drawn animation</a>, live-action, and <a href="/wiki/Computer_animation" title="Computer animation">computer animation</a>, May had to make sure that the costume would be the same throughout in terms of "color, <a href="/wiki/Shape" title="Shape">shape</a>, and texture".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HSB-2007nov15_30-4"><a href="#cite_note-HSB-2007nov15-30">[30]</a></sup> The costume for Narissa consisted of a leather corset and skirt, which looked "reptilian", as well as a <a href="/wiki/Cape" title="Cape">cape</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HSB-2007nov15_30-5"><a href="#cite_note-HSB-2007nov15-30">[30]</a></sup> Working with the animators, May incorporated parts of the <a href="/wiki/Dragon" title="Dragon">dragon</a>'s form into the costume; the cape was designed to look like <a href="/wiki/Wing" title="Wing">wings</a>, the <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/layer" title="wikt:layer">layers</a> of the skirt wrap around like a tail and a <a href="/wiki/Crown_(headgear)" title="Crown (headgear)">crown</a> that would turn into <a href="/wiki/Horn_(anatomy)" title="Horn (anatomy)">horns</a> during Narissa's transformation into a dragon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ThePlainDealer-2007nov23_28-5"><a href="#cite_note-ThePlainDealer-2007nov23-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enchanted_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Enchanted_(soundtrack)" title="Enchanted (soundtrack)">Enchanted (soundtrack)</a></div>
<p>The film's score was written by accomplished songwriter and composer <a href="/wiki/Alan_Menken" title="Alan Menken">Alan Menken</a>, who has worked on a number of <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Disney</a> films previously. Fellow composer <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Schwartz_(composer)" title="Stephen Schwartz (composer)">Stephen Schwartz</a> wrote the lyrics for six songs, also composed by Menken. Menken and Schwartz previously worked together on the songs for <i><a href="/wiki/Pocahontas_(1995_film)" title="Pocahontas (1995 film)">Pocahontas</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hunchback_of_Notre_Dame_(1996_film)" title="The Hunchback of Notre Dame (1996 film)">The Hunchback of Notre Dame</a></i>.</p>
<p>Menken became involved with the film in the early stages of the film's development and invited Schwartz to resume their collaboration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MO-music_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-MO-music-32">[32]</a></sup> They began the songwriting process by searching for the right moments in the story in which a song moment was allowed. Schwartz found that it was easier to justify situations in which the characters would burst into songs in <i>Enchanted</i> than in other live-action musicals as its concept "allowed the characters to sing in a way that was completely integral to the plot of the story."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MO-music_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-MO-music-32">[32]</a></sup> The three songs Giselle sings contain references to earlier Disney films. The first song played in the film, "True Love's Kiss", was written to be "a send-up of, and an homage to, the style of those Disney animated features", namely, "I'm Wishing" (<i><a href="/wiki/Snow_White_and_the_Seven_Dwarfs_(1937_film)" title="Snow White and the Seven Dwarfs (1937 film)">Snow White and the Seven Dwarfs</a></i>) and "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A_Dream_is_a_Wish_Your_Heart_Makes" title="A Dream is a Wish Your Heart Makes">A Dream is a Wish Your Heart Makes</a>" (<i><a href="/wiki/Cinderella_(1950_film)" title="Cinderella (1950 film)">Cinderella</a></i>), during which Disney heroines sing about the joy of being loved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Playbill-2007nov18_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Playbill-2007nov18-33">[33]</a></sup> It posed a challenge for Menken and <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Schwartz_(composer)" title="Stephen Schwartz (composer)">Schwartz</a> because of the "many preconceptions with that number"; it had to be reflective of the era of <i><a href="/wiki/Snow_White_and_the_Seven_Dwarfs_(1937_film)" title="Snow White and the Seven Dwarfs (1937 film)">Snow White and the Seven Dwarfs</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Cinderella_(1950_film)" title="Cinderella (1950 film)">Cinderella</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MO-music_32-2"><a href="#cite_note-MO-music-32">[32]</a></sup> Accordingly, Amy Adams performed the first song in an operetta style in contrast to the Broadway style of the later songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>Both "<a href="/wiki/Happy_Working_Song" title="Happy Working Song">Happy Working Song</a>" and "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/That%27s_How_You_Know_(musical_number)" title="That's How You Know (musical number)">That's How You Know</a>" also pay tributes to past Disney songs. "Happy Working Song" pays a lyrical homage to such songs as "<a href="/wiki/Whistle_While_You_Work" title="Whistle While You Work">Whistle While You Work</a>" (<i><a href="/wiki/Snow_White_and_the_Seven_Dwarfs_(1937_film)" title="Snow White and the Seven Dwarfs (1937 film)">Snow White and the Seven Dwarfs</a></i>), "The Work Song" (<i><a href="/wiki/Cinderella_(1950_film)" title="Cinderella (1950 film)">Cinderella</a></i>) "<a href="/wiki/A_Spoonful_of_Sugar" title="A Spoonful of Sugar">A Spoonful of Sugar</a>" (<i><a href="/wiki/Mary_Poppins_(film)" title="Mary Poppins (film)">Mary Poppins</a></i>) and “Making Christmas” (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Nightmare_Before_Christmas" title="The Nightmare Before Christmas">The Nightmare Before Christmas</a></i>), and a musical homage to the <a href="/wiki/Sherman_Brothers" title="Sherman Brothers">Sherman Brothers</a> (with a self-parodic "Alan Menken style" middle eight). "That's How You Know" is a self-parody of Menken's compositions for his Disney features, specifically such big production numbers as "<a href="/wiki/Under_the_Sea" title="Under the Sea">Under the Sea</a>" (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Little_Mermaid_(1989_film)" title="The Little Mermaid (1989 film)">The Little Mermaid</a></i>) and "<a href="/wiki/Be_Our_Guest" title="Be Our Guest">Be Our Guest</a>" (<i><a href="/wiki/Beauty_and_the_Beast_(1991_film)" title="Beauty and the Beast (1991 film)">Beauty and the Beast</a></i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Playbill-2007nov18_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-Playbill-2007nov18-33">[33]</a></sup> To achieve this, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Schwartz_(composer)" title="Stephen Schwartz (composer)">Schwartz</a> admitted he had to "push it a little bit further in terms of choices of words or certain lyrics" while maintaining "the classic Walt Disney sensibility".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MO-music_32-3"><a href="#cite_note-MO-music-32">[32]</a></sup> However, Menken noted that the songs he has written for Disney have always been "a little tongue-in-cheek".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MO-music_32-4"><a href="#cite_note-MO-music-32">[32]</a></sup> As the film progresses, the music uses more contemporary styles, which is heard through the adult ballad "<a href="/wiki/So_Close_(Jon_McLaughlin_song)" title="So Close (Jon McLaughlin song)">So Close</a>" and the country/pop number "Ever Ever After" (sung by <a href="/wiki/Carrie_Underwood" title="Carrie Underwood">Carrie Underwood</a> as a voice-over).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Playbill-2007nov18_33-2"><a href="#cite_note-Playbill-2007nov18-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>Out of the six completed songs written and composed by Menken and Schwartz, five remained in the finished film. The title song, "Enchanted," a duet featuring <a href="/wiki/Idina_Menzel" title="Idina Menzel">Idina Menzel</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Marsden" title="James Marsden">James Marsden</a>, was the only song of Menken's and Schwartz's authorship and composition that was deleted from the movie.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFWire-2007nov13_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-SFWire-2007nov13-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects">Effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enchanted_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The majority of the visual effects shots in <i>Enchanted</i> were done by <a href="/wiki/Tippett_Studio" title="Tippett Studio">Tippett Studio</a> in Berkeley, California, who contributed a total of 320 shots. These shots involved virtual sets, environmental effects and <a href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery" title="Computer-generated imagery">CG</a> characters that performed alongside real actors, namely the animated animals during the "Happy Working Song" sequence, Pip and the Narissa dragon during the live-action portions of the film. CIS Hollywood was responsible for 36 visual effects shots, which primarily dealt with <a href="/wiki/Wire_removal" title="Wire removal">wire removals</a> and composites. <a href="/wiki/Reel_FX_Creative_Studios" title="Reel FX Creative Studios">Reel FX Creative Studios</a> did four visual effects shots involving the pop-up book page-turn transitions while <a href="/wiki/Weta_Digital" title="Weta Digital">Weta Digital</a> did two.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VFXWorld-2007nov21_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-VFXWorld-2007nov21-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Out of all the animals that appear in the "<a href="/wiki/Happy_Working_Song" title="Happy Working Song">Happy Working Song</a>" sequence, the only real animals filmed on set were rats and pigeons. The real animals captured on film aided Tippett Studio in creating CG rats and pigeons, which gave dynamic performances such as having pigeons that carried brooms in their beaks and rats that scrubbed with toothbrushes. On the other hand, all the cockroaches were CG characters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCGSociety-2007dec4_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-TCGSociety-2007dec4-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pip, a chipmunk who can talk in the 2D world of Andalasia, loses his ability to communicate through speech in the real world so he must rely heavily on facial and body gestures. This meant the animators had to display Pip's emotions through performance as well as making him appear like a real chipmunk. The team at Tippett began the process of animating Pip by observing live chipmunks which were filmed in motion from "every conceivable angle", after which they created a photorealistic chipmunk through the use of 3D computer graphics software, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maya_(software)" title="Maya (software)">Maya</a> and Furrocious.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VFXWorld-2007nov21_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-VFXWorld-2007nov21-35">[35]</a></sup> When visual effects supervisor Thomas Schelesny showed the first animation of Pip to director Kevin Lima, he was surprised that he was a looking at CG character and not reference footage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LAT-2007dec02_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-LAT-2007dec02-37">[37]</a></sup> To enhance facial expressions, the modelers gave Pip eyebrows, which real chipmunks do not have.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCGSociety-2007dec4_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-TCGSociety-2007dec4-36">[36]</a></sup> During the filming of scenes in which Pip appears, a number of ways were used to indicate the physical presence of Pip. On some occasions, a small stuffed chipmunk with a wire armature on the inside was placed in the scene. In other situations, a rod with a small marker on the end or a laser pointer would be used to show the actors and cinematographer where Pip is.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VFXWorld-2007nov21_35-2"><a href="#cite_note-VFXWorld-2007nov21-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Unlike Pip, the Narissa dragon was allowed to be more of a fantasy character while still looking like a living character and a classic Disney villain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VFXWorld-2007nov21_35-3"><a href="#cite_note-VFXWorld-2007nov21-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LAT-2007dec02_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-LAT-2007dec02-37">[37]</a></sup> The CG dragon design was loosely based on a traditional Chinese dragon and Susan Sarandon's live-action witch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LAT-2007dec02_37-2"><a href="#cite_note-LAT-2007dec02-37">[37]</a></sup> When filming the scene which sees the transformation of Narissa from a woman into a dragon, a long pole was used to direct the extras' eyelines instead of a laser pointer. Set pieces were made to move back and forth in addition to having a computer-controlled lighting setup and a repeatable head on the camera that were all synchronized together. In the film's final sequence, in which Narissa climbs the <a href="/wiki/Woolworth_Building" title="Woolworth Building">Woolworth Building</a> while clutching Robert in her claws, a greenscreen rig was built to hold Patrick Dempsey in order to film his face and movements. The rig was a "puppeteering" approach that involved a robotic arm being controlled by three different floor effects artists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VFXWorld-2007nov21_35-4"><a href="#cite_note-VFXWorld-2007nov21-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enchanted_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The film was distributed by <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_Motion_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Studios Motion Pictures">Walt Disney Studios Motion Pictures</a> to 3,730 theaters in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hollywood-2007nov26_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-hollywood-2007nov26-38">[38]</a></sup> It was distributed worldwide by Walt Disney Studios Motion Pictures International to over 50 territories around the world<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> and topped the box office in several countries including the United Kingdom and Italy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> It is the first movie to be released under the Walt Disney Studios Motion Pictures name following the retirement of the previous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buena_Vista_Pictures_Distribution" title="Buena Vista Pictures Distribution">Buena Vista Pictures Distribution</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Merchandising">Merchandising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enchanted_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Merchandising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Disney had originally planned to add Giselle to the <a href="/wiki/Disney_Princess" title="Disney Princess">Disney Princess</a> line-up, as was shown at a 2007 Toy Fair where the Giselle doll was featured with packaging declaring her with Disney Princess status but decided against it when they realized they would have to pay for lifelong rights to <a href="/wiki/Amy_Adams" title="Amy Adams">Amy Adams</a>' image.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> While Giselle is not being marketed as one of the Disney Princesses, <i>Enchanted</i> merchandise was made available in various outlets with Adams' animated likeness being used on all Giselle merchandise. Giselle led the 2007 Hollywood Holly-Day Parade at <a href="/wiki/Disney%27s_Hollywood_Studios" title="Disney's Hollywood Studios">Disney's Hollywood Studios</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> She was also featured in the 2007 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_World_Christmas_Day_Parade" title="Walt Disney World Christmas Day Parade">Walt Disney World Christmas Day Parade</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Magic_Kingdom" title="Magic Kingdom">Magic Kingdom</a> with the official Disney Princesses.</p>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Enchanted_(video_game)" title="Enchanted (video game)">video game based on the film</a> was released for <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_DS" title="Nintendo DS">Nintendo DS</a> and mobile phones in addition to a <a href="/wiki/Game_Boy_Advance" title="Game Boy Advance">Game Boy Advance</a> title, <i>Enchanted: Once Upon Andalasia</i>, which is a prequel to the film, about Giselle and Pip rescuing Andalasia from a magic spell.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_media">Home media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enchanted_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Home media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Enchanted</i> was released on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc" title="Blu-ray Disc">Blu-ray Disc</a> and <a href="/wiki/DVD_player" title="DVD player">DVD</a> by <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_Home_Entertainment" title="Walt Disney Studios Home Entertainment">Walt Disney Studios Home Entertainment</a> on March 18, 2008, in the United States. While <i>Enchanted</i> topped the DVD sales chart on the week of its release in the United States, narrowly defeating the DVD sales of <i><a href="/wiki/I_Am_Legend_(film)" title="I Am Legend (film)">I Am Legend</a></i>, the Blu-ray Disc sales of <i>I Am Legend</i> were nearly four times the number of Blu-ray Disc sales of <i>Enchanted</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> The DVD was released in United Kingdom and Europe on April 7, 2008,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> and in Australia on May 21, 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>The bonus features included on both the DVD and Blu-ray Disc are "Fantasy Comes to Life", a three-part behind-the-scenes feature including "Happy Working Song", "That's How You Know" and "A Blast at the Ball"; six <a href="/wiki/Deleted_scene" title="Deleted scene">deleted scenes</a> with brief introductions by director Kevin Lima; bloopers; "Pip's Predicament: A Pop-Up Adventure", a short in pop-up storybook style; and Carrie Underwood's music video for "Ever Ever After".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Featured on the Blu-ray disc only is a trivia game titled "The D Files" that runs throughout the movie with high scoring players given access to videos "So Close", "Making Ever Ever After" and "True Love's Kiss".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> In the United States, certain DVDs at <a href="/wiki/Target_Corporation" title="Target Corporation">Target</a> stores contain a bonus DVD with a 30-minute-long making-of documentary titled <i>Becoming Enchanted: A New Classic Comes True</i>. This DVD is also sold with certain DVDs at <a href="/wiki/HMV" title="HMV">HMV</a> stores in the United Kingdom.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enchanted_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office_performance">Box office performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enchanted_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Box office performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Enchanted</i> earned $7,967,766 on the day of its release in the United States, placing at #1. It was also placed at #1 on Thanksgiving Day, earning $6,652,198 to bring its two-day total to $14.6 million. The film grossed $14.4 million on the following day, bringing its total haul to $29.0 million placing ahead of other contenders. <i>Enchanted</i> made $34.4 million on the Friday-Sunday period in 3,730 theaters for a per location average of $9,472 and $49.1 million over the five-day Thanksgiving holiday in 3,730 theaters for a per location average of $13,153.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hollywood-2007nov26_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-hollywood-2007nov26-38">[38]</a></sup> Its earnings over the five-day holiday exceeded projections by $7 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Ranking as the second-highest Thanksgiving opening after <i><a href="/wiki/Toy_Story_2" title="Toy Story 2">Toy Story 2</a></i>, which earned $80.1 million over the five-day holiday in 1999, <i>Enchanted</i> is the first film to open at #1 on the Thanksgiving frame in the 21st century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>In its second weekend, <i>Enchanted</i> was also the #1 film, grossing a further $16,403,316 at 3,730 locations for a per theater average of $4,397. It dropped to #2 in its third weekend, with a gross of $10,709,515 in 3,520 theaters for a per theater average of $3,042. It finished its fourth weekend at #4 with a gross of $5,533,884 in 3,066 locations for a per theater average of $1,804. <i>Enchanted</i> earned a gross of $127,807,262 in the United States and Canada as well a total of $340,487,652 worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOMojo_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-BOMojo-3">[3]</a></sup> It was the 15th highest grossing film worldwide released in 2007.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_response">Critical response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enchanted_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Critical response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of September 2014, the movie review aggregate website <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a> had tallied the film at an overall 93% approval rating (based on 187 reviews, with 174 "fresh" and 13 "rotten"),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a> gave it a rating of 75 out of 100 based on 32 reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Rotten Tomatoes ranked the film as the ninth best reviewed film in wide release of 2007 and named it the best family film of 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Amy_Adams_(actress).jpg"><img alt="Casual head shot of blue-eyed young woman with long reddish-blond hair pulled back." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="487" data-file-width="391" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Amy_Adams_%28actress%29.jpg/200px-Amy_Adams_%28actress%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Amy_Adams_%28actress%29.jpg/300px-Amy_Adams_%28actress%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b5/Amy_Adams_%28actress%29.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Amy_Adams_(actress).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Amy Adams received praise for her role as Giselle.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Positive reviews praised the film's take on a classic Disney story, its comedy and musical numbers as well as the performance of its lead actress, <a href="/wiki/Amy_Adams" title="Amy Adams">Amy Adams</a>. <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Sun-Times" title="Chicago Sun-Times">Chicago Sun-Times</a></i> gave the film three stars out of four, describing it as a "heart-winning musical comedy that skips lightly and sprightly from the lily pads of hope to the manhole covers of actuality" and one that "has a Disney willingness to allow fantasy into life".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Film critics of <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/LA_Weekly" title="LA Weekly">LA Weekly</a></i> remarked on the film's ability to cater for all ages. <i>LA Weekly</i> described the film as "the sort of buoyant, all-ages entertainment that Hollywood has been laboring to revive in recent years (most recently with <i><a href="/wiki/Hairspray_(2007_film)" title="Hairspray (2007 film)">Hairspray</a></i>) but hasn't managed to get right until now"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> while Todd McCarthy of <i>Variety</i> commented, "More than Disney's strictly animated product, <i>Enchanted</i>, in the manner of the vast majority of Hollywood films made until the '60s, is a film aimed at the entire population – niches be damned. It simply aims to please, without pandering, without vulgarity, without sops to pop-culture fads, and to pull this off today is no small feat."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Variety-2007nov18_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Variety-2007nov18-57">[57]</a></sup> <i>Enchanted</i> was the <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_Film_Critics_Association" title="Broadcast Film Critics Association">Broadcast Film Critics Association</a>'s choice for Best Family Film of 2007 while Carrie Rickey of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Philadelphia_Inquirer" title="The Philadelphia Inquirer">The Philadelphia Inquirer</a></i> named it the 4th best film of 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Premiere_(magazine)" title="Premiere (magazine)">Premiere</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Boston_Globe" title="The Boston Globe">The Boston Globe</a></i> all gave the film three out of four,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAToday-2007nov20-rev_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday-2007nov20-rev-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BostonGlobe-2007nov21_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-BostonGlobe-2007nov21-62">[62]</a></sup> while <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore_Sun" title="Baltimore Sun">Baltimore Sun</a></i> gave the film a B grade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BaltimoreSun-2007nov21_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-BaltimoreSun-2007nov21-63">[63]</a></sup> They cited that although the story is relatively predictable, the way in which the predictability of the film is part of the story, the amazingly extravagant musical numbers, along with the way in which Disney pokes fun at its traditional line of animated movies outweighs any squabbles about storyline or being unsure of what age bracket the film is made for. Michael Sragow of <i>Baltimore Sun</i> remarked that the film's "piquant idea and enough good jokes to overcome its uneven movie-making and uncertain tone",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BaltimoreSun-2007nov21_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-BaltimoreSun-2007nov21-63">[63]</a></sup> while Claudia Puig of <i>USA Today</i> stated that "though it's a fairly predictable fish-out-of-water tale (actually a princess-out-of-storybook saga), the casting is so perfect that it takes what could have been a ho-hum idea and renders it magical."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAToday-2007nov20-rev_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday-2007nov20-rev-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>Amy Adams herself garnered many favorable reviews. Reviewers praised her singing ability<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> and asserted that her performance, which was compared by some to her <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a>-nominated performance in <i><a href="/wiki/Junebug_(film)" title="Junebug (film)">Junebug</a></i>, has made Adams a movie star, likening it to <a href="/wiki/Mary_Poppins_(film)" title="Mary Poppins (film)"><i>Mary Poppins'</i></a> effect on <a href="/wiki/Julie_Andrews" title="Julie Andrews">Julie Andrews</a>' career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Variety-2007nov18_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-Variety-2007nov18-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BostonGlobe-2007nov21_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-BostonGlobe-2007nov21-62">[62]</a></sup> Similarly, film critics <a href="/wiki/Richard_Roeper" title="Richard Roeper">Richard Roeper</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michael_Phillips_(theatre_critic)" title="Michael Phillips (theatre critic)">Michael Phillips</a>, who gave the film positive reviews on <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/At_the_Movies_with_Ebert_%26_Roeper" title="At the Movies with Ebert &amp; Roeper">At the Movies with Ebert &amp; Roeper</a></i>, emphasized the effect of Adams' performance on the film with remarks like "Amy Adams is this movie" and "Amy Adams shows how to make a comic cliché work like magic." However, both agreed that the final sequence involving the computer-generated dragon "bogged down" the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Empire_(magazine)" title="Empire (magazine)">Empire</a></i> stated that the film was targeted at children but agreed with other reviewers that the "extremely game cast" was the film's best asset. It gave the film three out of five.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> <i>TIME</i> gave the film a C-, stating that the film "cannibalizes Walt's vault for jokes" and "fails to find a happy ending that doesn't feel two-dimensional".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Similarly, Peter Bradshaw of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> commented that the film "assumes a beady-eyed and deeply humourless sentimentality" and that Adams' performance was the "only decent thing in this overhyped family movie covered in a cellophane shrink-wrap of corporate Disney plastic-ness". Bradshaw gave the film two out of five.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accolades">Accolades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enchanted_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Accolades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
