<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Disney_references">Disney references</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enchanted_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Disney references">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Disney_references_in_Enchanted" title="List of Disney references in Enchanted">List of Disney references in Enchanted</a></div>
<p>According to director Kevin Lima, "thousands" of references are made to past and future works of Disney in <i>Enchanted</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> which serve as both a parody of and a "giant love letter to Disney classics".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TNYT-2007nov25_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-TNYT-2007nov25-84">[84]</a></sup> It took almost eight years for <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">Walt Disney Studios</a> to greenlight the production of the film because it "was always quite nervous about the tone in particular".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TNYT-2007nov25_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-TNYT-2007nov25-84">[84]</a></sup> As Lima worked with <a href="/wiki/Bill_Kelly_(writer)" title="Bill Kelly (writer)">Bill Kelly</a>, the writer, to inject Disney references to the plot, it became "an obsession"; he derived the name of every character as well as anything that needed a name from past Disney films to bring in more Disney references.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFW-2007nov20_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-SFW-2007nov20-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>While Disney animators have occasionally inserted a Disney character into background shots, for example, <a href="/wiki/Donald_Duck" title="Donald Duck">Donald Duck</a> appears in a crowd in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Little_Mermaid_(1989_film)" title="The Little Mermaid (1989 film)">The Little Mermaid</a></i>, they have avoided "mingling characters" from other Disney films for fear of weakening their individual mythologies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TNYT-2007nov25_84-2"><a href="#cite_note-TNYT-2007nov25-84">[84]</a></sup> In <i>Enchanted</i>, characters from past Disney films are openly seen, such as the appearances of <a href="/wiki/Thumper_(Bambi)" title="Thumper (Bambi)">Thumper</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flower_(Bambi)" title="Flower (Bambi)">Flower</a> from <i><a href="/wiki/Bambi" title="Bambi">Bambi</a></i> in the 2D animation portion of the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TNYT-2007nov25_84-3"><a href="#cite_note-TNYT-2007nov25-84">[84]</a></sup> Disney references are also made through camera work, <a href="/wiki/Set_construction" title="Set construction">sets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Costume" title="Costume">costumes</a>, music and dialogue. Obvious examples include the use of poisoned apples from <i><a href="/wiki/Snow_White_and_the_Seven_Dwarfs_(1937_film)" title="Snow White and the Seven Dwarfs (1937 film)">Snow White and the Seven Dwarfs</a></i> and True Love's Kiss from <i>Snow White</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Sleeping_Beauty_(1959_film)" title="Sleeping Beauty (1959 film)">Sleeping Beauty</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAToday-2007nov22-New_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday-2007nov22-New-13">[13]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dick_Cook" title="Dick Cook">Dick Cook</a>, the chairman of Walt Disney Studios, admitted that part of the goal of <i>Enchanted</i> was to create a new franchise (through the character of Giselle) and to revive the older ones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TNYT-2007nov25_84-4"><a href="#cite_note-TNYT-2007nov25-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sequel">Sequel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enchanted_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Sequel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In February 2010, <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i> reported that <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Walt Disney Pictures</a> planned to film a sequel with <a href="/wiki/Barry_Josephson" title="Barry Josephson">Barry Josephson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barry_Sonnenfeld" title="Barry Sonnenfeld">Barry Sonnenfeld</a> producing again. Jessie Nelson was attached to write the screenplay and <a href="/wiki/Anne_Fletcher" title="Anne Fletcher">Anne Fletcher</a> to direct. Disney hoped the cast members from the first film would return and for a release as early as 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>On January 12, 2011, composer <a href="/wiki/Alan_Menken" title="Alan Menken">Alan Menken</a> was asked about the sequel in an interview. His reply was, "I’ve heard things but there's nothing yet. I don’t know much about what’s happening with that. Honestly, I don’t know what the studio wants to do next. I presume there will be some future projects for me to work on. I love doing that, I really do. But I’m not frustrated that it isn’t one of them. At the moment I have a lot of stage things happening and I’m busy enough with that, so I really don’t need more on my plate."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>On March 28, 2011, in an interview for his latest film, <i><a href="/wiki/Hop_(film)" title="Hop (film)">Hop</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/James_Marsden" title="James Marsden">James Marsden</a> was asked about the sequel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>I don't know. I think that the clock is ticking on that one. <a href="/wiki/Amy_Adams" title="Amy Adams">Amy Adams</a> and I are both saying, "If there's going to be a sequel, we're not getting any younger." Since we play sort of ageless animated characters. Hopefully we do. That was something really special and I'd love to come back and do another. I've heard the same things you've heard. There's a script out there somewhere and there's talk of it, but I never believe it until I see the script and learned we're making that film. So I don't know. Too many eggs in that basket.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>As of July 2014, Disney had hired screenwriters J. David Stem and <a href="/wiki/David_N._Weiss" title="David N. Weiss">David N. Weiss</a> to write a script for a sequel and also hired <a href="/wiki/Anne_Fletcher" title="Anne Fletcher">Anne Fletcher</a> to direct the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> In October 2016, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">The Hollywood Reporter</a></i> reported that <a href="/wiki/Adam_Shankman" title="Adam Shankman">Adam Shankman</a> entered negotiations to direct the sequel, titled <i>Disenchanted</i>, and that Amy Adams would reprise her role with filming scheduled to begin in summer 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>

<th class="navbox-group" scope="row" style="padding-left:0;padding-right:0;">
<div style="padding:0em 0.75em;">Released</div>
</th>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
